المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة
بذلك النوع من التركيب دون غيره ( الثاني : ( من تلك الاحتمالات ( استناده) أي استناد المعجز ( إلى بعض الملائكة ) فإنها قادرة على أفعال غريبة فلعل ملكاً أظهر ما يعجز عنه البشر على يد المتنبي ليغوي الناس وأما عصمة الملائكة فإنما تعلم بقول فلا يمكن أن يتمسك بها هاهنا ) أو (الشياطين ) فإنها موجودة عندكم قادرة على أفعال خارقة ( أو ) استناده (إلى الاتصالات (الكوكبية ) وأنظارها الحادثة الحركات الفلكية (وهو) أي مدعي النبوة ( قد أحاط من صناعة النجامة بما لم يحط به غيره فاطلع على اتصال نادر لا يقع مثله إلا في ألوف من السنين ويستتبع أمراً غريباً ( فاتخذ ما علم وقوعه من الغرائب معجزاً لنفسه فلا يكون حينئذ دالاً على صدقه . ( الثالث : ( منها ( أن يكون ) الخارق الظاهر ) كرامة لا معجزة ) فلا يكون له دلالة على الصدق . ( الرابع : أن لا يصدق به التصديق ) أي سلمنا أن المعجز من تعالى لكنه ليس تصديقاً منه للمدعي ( إذ لا غرض واجباً ) للمدعي (إذ لا غرض واجباً) في أفعاله تعالى ( و) على تقدير وجوبه ( لا يتعين) التصديق له لكونه غرضاً من ذلك الخارق (إذ لعله ) أي الغرض منه ( غير التصديق ) له ( كإيهامه ) أي إيهام تصديقه ( ليحترز عنه بالاجتهاد فيثاب ) بذلك ) كإنزال المتشابهات ( فإنها بظواهرها توهم الخطأ ولا يمكن للمكلف الاحتراز عن ذلك الخطأ إلا بتحمل المشقة من التأمل الدقيق فيها فيستحق به الثواب ( أو ) يكون ذلك الخارق ( لتصديق نبي (آخر) موجود في جانب آخر أو يكون إرهاصاً لنبي سيأتي فيما بعد كالأحوال الظاهرة على النبي قبل مبعثه وكالنور الذي كان في جبين آبائه ( الخامس : أنه لا يلزم من تصديق الله ) إياه (صدقه إلا إذا علم استحالة الكذب على الله ولم يعلم ذلك عقلاً ( إذ لا يقبح عندكم منه شيء ) ولا سمعاً للزوم الدور السادس : لعل التحدي ) الصادر عن المدعي (لم يبلغ من هو قادر على المعارضة ) من الذين هم في بعض الأقطار، ( أو لعله ) أي القادر على المعارضة ( تركها مواضعة) مع المدعي ومواطأة معه ( في إعلاء كلمته لينال دولته حظاً) من وافراً . ( السابع : لعلهم استهانوا به (أولاً وظنوا أن دعوته مما لا يتم ولا يلتفت إليه فلم يشتغلوا بمعارضته في ابتداء أمره ) وخافوه آخر الشدة شوكته ) وكثرة أتباعه ( أو شغلهم ما يحتاجون إليه في تقويم معيشتهم عنه ) أي عن المدعي ومعارضته ( الثامن : لعله عوارض ولم يظهر لمانع منع المعارض عن إظهار ما عارض به ( أو ظهر ثم أخفاه أصحابه أي أتباع المدعي ( عند استيلائهم) وغلبتهم على الناس المخالفين لهم ( وطمسوا آثاره حتى انمحى بالكلية ) ومع قيام هذه الاحتمالات ) الثمانية ( لا يبقي لها أي للخارق الذي سمى معجزة ( دلالة على الصدق . الجواب الإجمالي ما قررناه غير مرة ) أي قررناه مراراً ومن جملتها جواب الطائفة الرابعة ( من أن التجويزات العقلية لا تنافي العلم العادي) كما في المحسوسات. (و) الجواب ( التفصيلي عن الأول أنا بينا أن لا مؤثرة في الوجود إلا الله فالمعجز لا يكون إلا فعلاً له لا للمدعي ) والسحر ونحوه إن لم يبلغ حد (الإعجاز الذي هو ( كفلق البحر وإحياء الموتى ) وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص ) كما هو مذهب جميع العقلاء فظاهر أنه لا يلتبس السحرة بالمعجزة فلا إشكال ( وإن بلغ ( السحر حد الإعجاز ( فإما ) أن يكون ( دون دعوى النبوة والتحدي فظاهر أيضاً أنه لا التباس (أو) يكون (معه) أي مع ادعاء النبوة والتحدي وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إما ) أن لا يخلقه الله على يده أو أن يقدر غيره على معارضته وإلا كان تصديقاً للكاذب وإنه محال ) على الله سبحانه لكونه كذباً . ( و ) الجواب ( عن الثاني أن لا خالق إلا الله فلا يكون المعجز مستنداً إلى غير ) وعن الثالث : إن ( لم يجوز الكرامة فلا إشكال عليه و ( من جوزها فقال بعضهم منهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق : لا تبلغ الكرامة الظاهرة على يد الأولياء (درجة المعجز، وقيل: لا تقع الكرامة ( على القصد والاختيار حتى إذا أراد الولي إيقاعها لم تقع بل وقوعها اتفاقي فقط ) وقال القاضي : تجوز الكرامة (إذ لم تقع على طريق التعظيم والجلال لأن ذلك ليس من شعار الصالحين ومع ذلك تمتاز ) الكرامة عن المعجز ( بأنها مع دعوى الولاية دون النبوة وعلى التقادير كلها ( فالفرق بينها وبين المعجزة ظاهر) فلا تشتبه إحداهما بالأخرى. وعن الرابع: إنا لا نقول بالغرض ) أي لأنا نقول بأن خلق المعجزة لغرض التصديق لأن أفعاله تعالى عندنا غير معللة بالأغراض ( بل نقول : ( إن خلقها على يد المدعي ( يدل على تصديق له قائم بذاته تعالى كما أن حمرة الخجل تفيد العلم الضروري بحصول الخجلة مع جواز حصولها بدونها أما على القول باستناد الحوادث إلى القادر المختار فظاهر وأما على القول بالموجب فلأنه يجوز أن يحدث شكل غريب سماوي يقتضي تلك الحمرة في ذلك الشخص من غير أن يحصل فيه الخجالة ( وعن الخامس : فقد مر في مسألة الكلام من موقف الإلهيات امتناع الكذب عليه سبحانه وتعالى . ( وعن السادس : إذا قوله : (وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إلخ ) يمكن أن يقال : لا حاجة إلى شيء منهما لجواز أن يخلق الله تعالى العلم الضروري بكذبه أو ينصب أمارات دالة على كذبه بحيث يعلم منها قطعاً .
قوله : (لا) تبلغ الكرامة درجة (المعجزة هذا مردود بأن من جملة المعجزات علم الغيب وإحياء الموتى، وقد روى مثل ذلك عن كثير من السلف. ولذا قيل إن الأمة مرآة نبيهم فما وقع معجزة للنبي عليه السلام صح مثله كرامة لأمته إذا كانت على طريقته .
The First Observatory - The Third Purpose: On the possibility of the mission. By that type of composition without other. (Second: Among those possibilities: its attribution, i.e., the attribution of the miracle to some angels, for they are capable of strange acts. Perhaps an angel manifested what humans are incapable of at the hand of the claimant to prophethood to mislead the people. As for the infallibility of angels, it is known only by scripture, so it cannot be relied upon here. Or to the devils, for they exist according to you, capable of extraordinary acts. Or its attribution to astrological conjunctions and their effects from the motions of the celestial spheres, and he (the claimant to prophethood) has encompassed the art of astrology beyond others, so he becomes aware of a rare conjunction that occurs only once in thousands of years and entails a strange event, and then he takes that which he knows will occur from among the strange events as a miracle for himself, so it is not then indicative of his truthfulness. (Third: Among them is that the apparent extraordinary act is a miracle of saints (karama) not a miracle (mu'jiza), so it has no indication of truthfulness. (Fourth: That the confirmation (tasdiq) is not accompanied by it, i.e., we grant that the miracle is from God, but it is not a confirmation from Him for the claimant, for there is no necessary purpose for the claimant, since there is no necessary purpose in His acts, and on the assumption of its necessity, the confirmation is not determined to be the purpose of that extraordinary act, for perhaps its purpose is other than confirmation, such as making it appear as confirmation so that one may be cautious of it through exertion and thus be rewarded, like the sending down of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat), for their apparent meanings suggest error, and the accountable person cannot avoid that error except by bearing the difficulty of precise reflection on them, thereby deserving reward. Or that extraordinary act is for confirming another prophet existing on another side, or it is a foretelling (irhas) for a prophet to come later, like the conditions appearing upon the prophet before his mission and the light that was on the foreheads of his ancestors. (Fifth: That the confirmation of God of him does not entail his truthfulness unless one knows that lying is impossible for God, and that is not known rationally (for according to you nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation due to circularity. (Sixth: Perhaps the challenge (tahaddi) issued by the claimant did not reach those capable of opposition among those in some regions, or perhaps the capable one abandoned it out of collusion with the claimant in promoting his word, so that his state would gain abundant fortune. (Seventh: Perhaps they underestimated him initially, thinking his call would not succeed and would not be paid attention to, so they did not occupy themselves with opposing him at the beginning of his affair, and they feared him later due to the severity of his power and the multitude of his followers, or they were occupied with what they needed for their livelihood away from him. (Eighth: Perhaps there were obstacles and the opponent did not appear due to a hindrance preventing him from showing his opposition, or he appeared and then his companions, i.e., the followers of the claimant, hid it when they prevailed and overcame the opposing people, and obliterated its traces until it was completely erased. And with the existence of these eight possibilities, there remains no indication of truthfulness for the extraordinary act called a miracle. The summary answer is what we have established more than once, i.e., we have established it repeatedly, including the answer of the fourth group: that rational possibilities do not contradict ordinary knowledge, as in sense-perceptibles. And the detailed answer to the first: we have shown that there is no effective agent in existence except God, so the miracle can only be an act of His, not of the claimant. And magic and the like, if they do not reach the level of inimitability (i'jaz) which is like splitting the sea and reviving the dead and healing the blind and leprous, as is the doctrine of all rational people, then it is apparent that magicians are not confused with miracle, so no problem. And if magic reaches the level of inimitability, then either it is without the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then it is also apparent that there is no confusion, or it is with it, i.e., with the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then one of two things is unavoidable: either God does not create it at his hand, or He empowers someone else to oppose it; otherwise, it would be confirmation of a liar, and that is impossible for God, being falsehood. And the answer to the second: there is no creator except God, so the miracle cannot be attributed to other than Him. And about the third: if one does not allow miracles of saints (karama), then no problem; and for those who allow it, some said, including al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq: the karama apparent at the hand of saints does not reach the degree of the miracle; and it was said: karama does not occur intentionally and voluntarily, such that if the saint wants to perform it, it does not happen, rather its occurrence is only accidental. And al-Qadi said: karama is allowed, since it does not occur in the way of glorification and majesty, because that is not the character of the righteous; nevertheless, the karama is distinguished from the mu'jiza by being with the claim of sainthood (wilaya) not prophethood. And according to all the positions, the difference between them and the miracle is apparent, so one is not confused with the other. And about the fourth: we do not say purpose, i.e., we do not say that the creation of the miracle is for the purpose of confirmation, because His acts are not caused by purposes according to us; rather we say: its creation at the hand of the claimant indicates a confirmation for him subsisting in God's essence, just as the redness of embarrassment yields necessary knowledge of the occurrence of embarrassment, even though it is possible for it to occur without it. This is clear on the doctrine of attributing events to the free chooser; as for the doctrine of necessitation (al-mujib), it is possible that a strange celestial figure occurs necessitating that redness in that person without the occurrence of embarrassment in him. And about the fifth: it has already passed in the issue of speech (kalam) from the stand of divinity the impossibility of lying upon Him, exalted and high. And about the sixth: then his saying: (Then one of two things is unavoidable, etc.) It can be said: there is no need for either of them, because it is possible that God creates necessary knowledge of his lying or sets up indicators indicating his lying such that one knows it definitively. His saying: (No) the karama reaches the degree of the miracle. This is refuted by the fact that among the miracles are knowledge of the unseen and reviving the dead, and that has been narrated from many of the predecessors. Hence it is said: the community is the mirror of their prophet, so whatever occurred as a miracle for the prophet, peace be upon him, its like is valid as a karama for his community if they are upon his path.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation of eight objections (shubuhāt) against the probative force of miracles (mu‘jizāt) in establishing the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood, followed by a general refutation and then detailed answers to each objection. The author first lists the objections sequentially:
1. (Second objection, since the first is on a previous page) The miracle might be attributable to angels or devils performing extraordinary acts, or to astrological knowledge enabling the claimant to predict a rare event.
2. The extraordinary act might be a saintly miracle (karāma) rather than a prophetic miracle.
3. The miracle does not necessarily carry God's confirmation (taṣdīq) because God has no necessary purpose; it could be meant to test people (like ambiguous verses) or to confirm another prophet or to be a foretelling.
4. God's confirmation does not entail the claimant's truthfulness unless we know that lying is impossible for God, which is not known rationally (since nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation (circular).
5. The challenge (taḥaddī) may not have reached capable opponents, or they colluded with the claimant.
6. People may have initially underestimated him and then feared his power, or were preoccupied.
7. Obstacles may have prevented opposition, or opponents' works were suppressed.
The objector concludes that with these possibilities, miracles lose their probative value.

The general answer (al-jawāb al-ijmālī) states that rational possibilities (tajwīzāt) do not negate ordinary certainty (al-‘ilm al-‘ādī), just as in the case of sense-perceptibles.

Then detailed answers follow:
- To the first: Only God is the true agent; magic, unless it reaches the level of inimitability and is claimed with challenge, does not confuse; if it does, God either prevents it or enables opposition, otherwise it would be confirming a liar, which is impossible.
- To the second: Only God creates; miracles cannot be from other than Him.
- To the third: If karāma is denied, no problem; if allowed, it is lesser or unintentional or not in a manner of glorification, and is distinct by being linked to sainthood not prophethood.
- To the fourth: Actions of God are not purpose-driven; the miracle indicates confirmation inherently, like blushing indicates embarrassment.
- To the fifth: The impossibility of lying about God has been established earlier.
- To the sixth: It is possible that God gives necessary knowledge of the claimant's falsity without needing opposition.
The passage ends with a marginal remark refuting the claim that karāma cannot reach the level of mu‘jiza, citing examples from the Salaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are always clear signs of divine confirmation.
Correction: The objections show that miracles could have non-divine or ambiguous origins, so they require further analysis.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth doubt, what could be an alternative purpose for a miracle besides confirming the claimant?
A) To demonstrate the claimant's power
B) To test the people (like ambiguous verses)
C) To terrify the opponents
D) To show the superiority of the prophet

Key Takeaway
The first four doubts challenge the divine origin and confirmatory intent of miracles, requiring careful refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about an extraordinary event claimed as a miracle, do you immediately accept it as a divine sign, or do you pause to consider the four alternatives mentioned by al-Qushji? Which of these doubts have you never considered before, and why? Commit to examining such claims more critically from now on.
?
The fourth doubt asserts that we cannot rationally know that God cannot lie—so how do you personally ground your certainty that a prophetic claim confirmed by a miracle must be true? Does this question unsettle your faith? If so, what is the real basis of your trust in God's truthfulness?
?
If a miracle could be from angels, devils, or saints, how do you distinguish a true prophetic miracle from these other possibilities? Have you ever attributed a blessed event in your life to a saint's karama without considering whether it might be from God for a different purpose? Search your heart: are you more attached to the messenger or to the Message?

Prophethood

Last Four Doubts and Their Cumulative Effect
Al-Qushji lists the final four doubts and concludes they undermine the miracle's probative value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the remaining four objections: the challenge may not reach opponents, collusion, initial neglect followed by fear, and suppression of opposing miracles.

Core Idea
Even if a miracle is genuine, human factors can prevent it from proving truthfulness.

The final four doubts shift focus from the miracle itself to the circumstances surrounding it. They argue that the challenge (tahaddi) might not have reached capable opponents, or they colluded, or they were initially indifferent, or later suppressed evidence. These possibilities, if valid, would undermine the miracle's probative force.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the last four doubts
Read the Arabic and translation. Note how each doubt appeals to practical human conditions: distance, collusion, neglect, and suppression.
These are objections six through eight in the original.
2
Analyze each doubt's logical structure
For each, identify the condition that could break the link between miracle and truth. The sixth doubts the reach of the challenge. The seventh doubts the response due to underestimation or occupation. The eighth doubts the preservation of evidence.
3
Assess the cumulative argument
The objector concludes that with all eight possibilities, the miracle loses its indication. Consider how these human factors together create uncertainty.
The refutation will address each.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة

( الثالث : ( منها ( أن يكون ) الخارق الظاهر ) كرامة لا معجزة ) فلا يكون له دلالة على الصدق . ( الرابع : أن لا يصدق به التصديق ) أي سلمنا أن المعجز من تعالى لكنه ليس تصديقاً منه للمدعي ( إذ لا غرض واجباً ) للمدعي (إذ لا غرض واجباً) في أفعاله تعالى ( و) على تقدير وجوبه ( لا يتعين) التصديق له لكونه غرضاً من ذلك الخارق (إذ لعله ) أي الغرض منه ( غير التصديق ) له ( كإيهامه ) أي إيهام تصديقه ( ليحترز عنه بالاجتهاد فيثاب ) بذلك ) كإنزال المتشابهات ( فإنها بظواهرها توهم الخطأ ولا يمكن للمكلف الاحتراز عن ذلك الخطأ إلا بتحمل المشقة من التأمل الدقيق فيها فيستحق به الثواب ( أو ) يكون ذلك الخارق ( لتصديق نبي (آخر) موجود في جانب آخر أو يكون إرهاصاً لنبي سيأتي فيما بعد كالأحوال الظاهرة على النبي قبل مبعثه وكالنور الذي كان في جبين آبائه ( الخامس : أنه لا يلزم من تصديق الله ) إياه (صدقه إلا إذا علم استحالة الكذب على الله ولم يعلم ذلك عقلاً ( إذ لا يقبح عندكم منه شيء ) ولا سمعاً للزوم الدور السادس : لعل التحدي ) الصادر عن المدعي (لم يبلغ من هو قادر على المعارضة ) من الذين هم في بعض الأقطار، ( أو لعله ) أي القادر على المعارضة ( تركها مواضعة) مع المدعي ومواطأة معه ( في إعلاء كلمته لينال دولته حظاً) من وافراً . ( السابع : لعلهم استهانوا به (أولاً وظنوا أن دعوته مما لا يتم ولا يلتفت إليه فلم يشتغلوا بمعارضته في ابتداء أمره ) وخافوه آخر الشدة شوكته ) وكثرة أتباعه ( أو شغلهم ما يحتاجون إليه في تقويم معيشتهم عنه ) أي عن المدعي ومعارضته ( الثامن : لعله عوارض ولم يظهر لمانع منع المعارض عن إظهار ما عارض به ( أو ظهر ثم أخفاه أصحابه أي أتباع المدعي ( عند استيلائهم) وغلبتهم على الناس المخالفين لهم ( وطمسوا آثاره حتى انمحى بالكلية ) ومع قيام هذه الاحتمالات ) الثمانية ( لا يبقي لها أي للخارق الذي سمى معجزة ( دلالة على الصدق . الجواب الإجمالي ما قررناه غير مرة ) أي قررناه مراراً ومن جملتها جواب الطائفة الرابعة ( من أن التجويزات العقلية لا تنافي العلم العادي) كما في المحسوسات. (و) الجواب ( التفصيلي عن الأول أنا بينا أن لا مؤثرة في الوجود إلا الله فالمعجز لا يكون إلا فعلاً له لا للمدعي ) والسحر ونحوه إن لم يبلغ حد (الإعجاز الذي هو ( كفلق البحر وإحياء الموتى ) وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص ) كما هو مذهب جميع العقلاء فظاهر أنه لا يلتبس السحرة بالمعجزة فلا إشكال ( وإن بلغ ( السحر حد الإعجاز ( فإما ) أن يكون ( دون دعوى النبوة والتحدي فظاهر أيضاً أنه لا التباس (أو) يكون (معه) أي مع ادعاء النبوة والتحدي وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إما ) أن لا يخلقه الله على يده أو أن يقدر غيره على معارضته وإلا كان تصديقاً للكاذب وإنه محال ) على الله سبحانه لكونه كذباً . ( و ) الجواب ( عن الثاني أن لا خالق إلا الله فلا يكون المعجز مستنداً إلى غير ) وعن الثالث : إن ( لم يجوز الكرامة فلا إشكال عليه و ( من جوزها فقال بعضهم منهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق : لا تبلغ الكرامة الظاهرة على يد الأولياء (درجة المعجز، وقيل: لا تقع الكرامة ( على القصد والاختيار حتى إذا أراد الولي إيقاعها لم تقع بل وقوعها اتفاقي فقط ) وقال القاضي : تجوز الكرامة (إذ لم تقع على طريق التعظيم والجلال لأن ذلك ليس من شعار الصالحين ومع ذلك تمتاز ) الكرامة عن المعجز ( بأنها مع دعوى الولاية دون النبوة وعلى التقادير كلها ( فالفرق بينها وبين المعجزة ظاهر) فلا تشتبه إحداهما بالأخرى. وعن الرابع: إنا لا نقول بالغرض ) أي لأنا نقول بأن خلق المعجزة لغرض التصديق لأن أفعاله تعالى عندنا غير معللة بالأغراض ( بل نقول : ( إن خلقها على يد المدعي ( يدل على تصديق له قائم بذاته تعالى كما أن حمرة الخجل تفيد العلم الضروري بحصول الخجلة مع جواز حصولها بدونها أما على القول باستناد الحوادث إلى القادر المختار فظاهر وأما على القول بالموجب فلأنه يجوز أن يحدث شكل غريب سماوي يقتضي تلك الحمرة في ذلك الشخص من غير أن يحصل فيه الخجالة ( وعن الخامس : فقد مر في مسألة الكلام من موقف الإلهيات امتناع الكذب عليه سبحانه وتعالى . ( وعن السادس : إذا قوله : (وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إلخ ) يمكن أن يقال : لا حاجة إلى شيء منهما لجواز أن يخلق الله تعالى العلم الضروري بكذبه أو ينصب أمارات دالة على كذبه بحيث يعلم منها قطعاً .
قوله : (لا) تبلغ الكرامة درجة (المعجزة هذا مردود بأن من جملة المعجزات علم الغيب وإحياء الموتى، وقد روى مثل ذلك عن كثير من السلف. ولذا قيل إن الأمة مرآة نبيهم فما وقع معجزة للنبي عليه السلام صح مثله كرامة لأمته إذا كانت على طريقته .
The First Observatory - The Third Purpose: On the possibility of the mission. By that type of composition without other. (Second: Among those possibilities: its attribution, i.e., the attribution of the miracle to some angels, for they are capable of strange acts. Perhaps an angel manifested what humans are incapable of at the hand of the claimant to prophethood to mislead the people. As for the infallibility of angels, it is known only by scripture, so it cannot be relied upon here. Or to the devils, for they exist according to you, capable of extraordinary acts. Or its attribution to astrological conjunctions and their effects from the motions of the celestial spheres, and he (the claimant to prophethood) has encompassed the art of astrology beyond others, so he becomes aware of a rare conjunction that occurs only once in thousands of years and entails a strange event, and then he takes that which he knows will occur from among the strange events as a miracle for himself, so it is not then indicative of his truthfulness. (Third: Among them is that the apparent extraordinary act is a miracle of saints (karama) not a miracle (mu'jiza), so it has no indication of truthfulness. (Fourth: That the confirmation (tasdiq) is not accompanied by it, i.e., we grant that the miracle is from God, but it is not a confirmation from Him for the claimant, for there is no necessary purpose for the claimant, since there is no necessary purpose in His acts, and on the assumption of its necessity, the confirmation is not determined to be the purpose of that extraordinary act, for perhaps its purpose is other than confirmation, such as making it appear as confirmation so that one may be cautious of it through exertion and thus be rewarded, like the sending down of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat), for their apparent meanings suggest error, and the accountable person cannot avoid that error except by bearing the difficulty of precise reflection on them, thereby deserving reward. Or that extraordinary act is for confirming another prophet existing on another side, or it is a foretelling (irhas) for a prophet to come later, like the conditions appearing upon the prophet before his mission and the light that was on the foreheads of his ancestors. (Fifth: That the confirmation of God of him does not entail his truthfulness unless one knows that lying is impossible for God, and that is not known rationally (for according to you nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation due to circularity. (Sixth: Perhaps the challenge (tahaddi) issued by the claimant did not reach those capable of opposition among those in some regions, or perhaps the capable one abandoned it out of collusion with the claimant in promoting his word, so that his state would gain abundant fortune. (Seventh: Perhaps they underestimated him initially, thinking his call would not succeed and would not be paid attention to, so they did not occupy themselves with opposing him at the beginning of his affair, and they feared him later due to the severity of his power and the multitude of his followers, or they were occupied with what they needed for their livelihood away from him. (Eighth: Perhaps there were obstacles and the opponent did not appear due to a hindrance preventing him from showing his opposition, or he appeared and then his companions, i.e., the followers of the claimant, hid it when they prevailed and overcame the opposing people, and obliterated its traces until it was completely erased. And with the existence of these eight possibilities, there remains no indication of truthfulness for the extraordinary act called a miracle. The summary answer is what we have established more than once, i.e., we have established it repeatedly, including the answer of the fourth group: that rational possibilities do not contradict ordinary knowledge, as in sense-perceptibles. And the detailed answer to the first: we have shown that there is no effective agent in existence except God, so the miracle can only be an act of His, not of the claimant. And magic and the like, if they do not reach the level of inimitability (i'jaz) which is like splitting the sea and reviving the dead and healing the blind and leprous, as is the doctrine of all rational people, then it is apparent that magicians are not confused with miracle, so no problem. And if magic reaches the level of inimitability, then either it is without the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then it is also apparent that there is no confusion, or it is with it, i.e., with the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then one of two things is unavoidable: either God does not create it at his hand, or He empowers someone else to oppose it; otherwise, it would be confirmation of a liar, and that is impossible for God, being falsehood. And the answer to the second: there is no creator except God, so the miracle cannot be attributed to other than Him. And about the third: if one does not allow miracles of saints (karama), then no problem; and for those who allow it, some said, including al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq: the karama apparent at the hand of saints does not reach the degree of the miracle; and it was said: karama does not occur intentionally and voluntarily, such that if the saint wants to perform it, it does not happen, rather its occurrence is only accidental. And al-Qadi said: karama is allowed, since it does not occur in the way of glorification and majesty, because that is not the character of the righteous; nevertheless, the karama is distinguished from the mu'jiza by being with the claim of sainthood (wilaya) not prophethood. And according to all the positions, the difference between them and the miracle is apparent, so one is not confused with the other. And about the fourth: we do not say purpose, i.e., we do not say that the creation of the miracle is for the purpose of confirmation, because His acts are not caused by purposes according to us; rather we say: its creation at the hand of the claimant indicates a confirmation for him subsisting in God's essence, just as the redness of embarrassment yields necessary knowledge of the occurrence of embarrassment, even though it is possible for it to occur without it. This is clear on the doctrine of attributing events to the free chooser; as for the doctrine of necessitation (al-mujib), it is possible that a strange celestial figure occurs necessitating that redness in that person without the occurrence of embarrassment in him. And about the fifth: it has already passed in the issue of speech (kalam) from the stand of divinity the impossibility of lying upon Him, exalted and high. And about the sixth: then his saying: (Then one of two things is unavoidable, etc.) It can be said: there is no need for either of them, because it is possible that God creates necessary knowledge of his lying or sets up indicators indicating his lying such that one knows it definitively. His saying: (No) the karama reaches the degree of the miracle. This is refuted by the fact that among the miracles are knowledge of the unseen and reviving the dead, and that has been narrated from many of the predecessors. Hence it is said: the community is the mirror of their prophet, so whatever occurred as a miracle for the prophet, peace be upon him, its like is valid as a karama for his community if they are upon his path.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation of eight objections (shubuhāt) against the probative force of miracles (mu‘jizāt) in establishing the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood, followed by a general refutation and then detailed answers to each objection. The author first lists the objections sequentially:
1. (Second objection, since the first is on a previous page) The miracle might be attributable to angels or devils performing extraordinary acts, or to astrological knowledge enabling the claimant to predict a rare event.
2. The extraordinary act might be a saintly miracle (karāma) rather than a prophetic miracle.
3. The miracle does not necessarily carry God's confirmation (taṣdīq) because God has no necessary purpose; it could be meant to test people (like ambiguous verses) or to confirm another prophet or to be a foretelling.
4. God's confirmation does not entail the claimant's truthfulness unless we know that lying is impossible for God, which is not known rationally (since nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation (circular).
5. The challenge (taḥaddī) may not have reached capable opponents, or they colluded with the claimant.
6. People may have initially underestimated him and then feared his power, or were preoccupied.
7. Obstacles may have prevented opposition, or opponents' works were suppressed.
The objector concludes that with these possibilities, miracles lose their probative value.

The general answer (al-jawāb al-ijmālī) states that rational possibilities (tajwīzāt) do not negate ordinary certainty (al-‘ilm al-‘ādī), just as in the case of sense-perceptibles.

Then detailed answers follow:
- To the first: Only God is the true agent; magic, unless it reaches the level of inimitability and is claimed with challenge, does not confuse; if it does, God either prevents it or enables opposition, otherwise it would be confirming a liar, which is impossible.
- To the second: Only God creates; miracles cannot be from other than Him.
- To the third: If karāma is denied, no problem; if allowed, it is lesser or unintentional or not in a manner of glorification, and is distinct by being linked to sainthood not prophethood.
- To the fourth: Actions of God are not purpose-driven; the miracle indicates confirmation inherently, like blushing indicates embarrassment.
- To the fifth: The impossibility of lying about God has been established earlier.
- To the sixth: It is possible that God gives necessary knowledge of the claimant's falsity without needing opposition.
The passage ends with a marginal remark refuting the claim that karāma cannot reach the level of mu‘jiza, citing examples from the Salaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mere existence of a miracle is sufficient to prove prophethood regardless of context.
Correction: The objections show that contextual factors (reach of challenge, collusion, suppression) can create doubt, so context must be examined.

Checkpoint
According to the eighth doubt, what could happen to evidence of opposition?
A) It is preserved by historians
B) It is hidden or destroyed by the claimant's followers
C) It is dismissed as irrelevant
D) It is used to prove the claimant's truth

Key Takeaway
The final four doubts highlight how human circumstances can prevent a miracle from being a clear proof, but these are all merely possible, not actual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter the clear signs of prophethood in the Qur'an and the miracles of the Prophet, do you ever catch yourself coming up with excuses—like 'maybe it was just a trick' or 'people were easily fooled back then'—to avoid the personal demand that those signs place on you? What would it take for you to drop those excuses today?
?
The objector suggests that opponents may have colluded with the claimant for worldly gain. Examine your own heart: are there any worldly attachments—status, comfort, relationships—that are making you 'collude' with falsehood or resist the truth? Will you commit to identifying one such attachment this week and begin to detach from it?
?
If the miracle's probative value can be undermined by mere possibilities, what does that say about your own willingness to accept the truth? Are you holding onto 'possible' doubts as a shield to avoid submitting to Allah? What would it mean for your prayer life, your character, and your purpose if you let go of those doubts and embraced the certainty that the Prophet's message is from Allah?

General and Detailed Refutations (Part 1)
Al-Qushji gives a general epistemological answer and detailed refutations of the first four doubts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general answer (rational possibilities do not negate ordinary certainty) and the detailed refutations of the first four objections.

Core Idea
Rational possibilities do not destroy the ordinary certainty we have about miracles, just as they don't for sense-perceptibles.

Having presented the eight objections, Al-Qushji now refutes them. He gives a general answer that applies to all: rational possibilities (tajwizat) do not contradict ordinary certainty (al-'ilm al-'adi). Then he answers each doubt in detail. In this lesson, we cover the general answer and the refutations of the first four doubts.

Guided Path
1
Read the general answer
The general answer states that just as we accept sense-perceptibles despite logical possibilities of error, we accept the probative value of miracles despite these possibilities.
This is a key principle in kalam epistemology.
2
Follow the detailed refutations for doubts 1-4
Read each refutation carefully. Note how the author responds to each objection: for the first, he denies any effective agent but God; for the second, he emphasizes God as sole creator; for the third, he distinguishes karama from mu'jiza; for the fourth, he denies that God's acts have purposes and gives an analogy.
The refutations are concise and logical.
3
Reflect on the coherence
Consider how the general answer and specific answers work together to restore confidence in the miracle as a proof.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة
بذلك النوع من التركيب دون غيره ( الثاني : ( من تلك الاحتمالات ( استناده) أي استناد المعجز ( إلى بعض الملائكة ) فإنها قادرة على أفعال غريبة فلعل ملكاً أظهر ما يعجز عنه البشر على يد المتنبي ليغوي الناس وأما عصمة الملائكة فإنما تعلم بقول فلا يمكن أن يتمسك بها هاهنا ) أو (الشياطين ) فإنها موجودة عندكم قادرة على أفعال خارقة ( أو ) استناده (إلى الاتصالات (الكوكبية ) وأنظارها الحادثة الحركات الفلكية (وهو) أي مدعي النبوة ( قد أحاط من صناعة النجامة بما لم يحط به غيره فاطلع على اتصال نادر لا يقع مثله إلا في ألوف من السنين ويستتبع أمراً غريباً ( فاتخذ ما علم وقوعه من الغرائب معجزاً لنفسه فلا يكون حينئذ دالاً على صدقه . ( الثالث : ( منها ( أن يكون ) الخارق الظاهر ) كرامة لا معجزة ) فلا يكون له دلالة على الصدق . ( الرابع : أن لا يصدق به التصديق ) أي سلمنا أن المعجز من تعالى لكنه ليس تصديقاً منه للمدعي ( إذ لا غرض واجباً ) للمدعي (إذ لا غرض واجباً) في أفعاله تعالى ( و) على تقدير وجوبه ( لا يتعين) التصديق له لكونه غرضاً من ذلك الخارق (إذ لعله ) أي الغرض منه ( غير التصديق ) له ( كإيهامه ) أي إيهام تصديقه ( ليحترز عنه بالاجتهاد فيثاب ) بذلك ) كإنزال المتشابهات ( فإنها بظواهرها توهم الخطأ ولا يمكن للمكلف الاحتراز عن ذلك الخطأ إلا بتحمل المشقة من التأمل الدقيق فيها فيستحق به الثواب ( أو ) يكون ذلك الخارق ( لتصديق نبي (آخر) موجود في جانب آخر أو يكون إرهاصاً لنبي سيأتي فيما بعد كالأحوال الظاهرة على النبي قبل مبعثه وكالنور الذي كان في جبين آبائه ( الخامس : أنه لا يلزم من تصديق الله ) إياه (صدقه إلا إذا علم استحالة الكذب على الله ولم يعلم ذلك عقلاً ( إذ لا يقبح عندكم منه شيء ) ولا سمعاً للزوم الدور السادس : لعل التحدي ) الصادر عن المدعي (لم يبلغ من هو قادر على المعارضة ) من الذين هم في بعض الأقطار، ( أو لعله ) أي القادر على المعارضة ( تركها مواضعة) مع المدعي ومواطأة معه ( في إعلاء كلمته لينال دولته حظاً) من وافراً . ( السابع : لعلهم استهانوا به (أولاً وظنوا أن دعوته مما لا يتم ولا يلتفت إليه فلم يشتغلوا بمعارضته في ابتداء أمره ) وخافوه آخر الشدة شوكته ) وكثرة أتباعه ( أو شغلهم ما يحتاجون إليه في تقويم معيشتهم عنه ) أي عن المدعي ومعارضته ( الثامن : لعله عوارض ولم يظهر لمانع منع المعارض عن إظهار ما عارض به ( أو ظهر ثم أخفاه أصحابه أي أتباع المدعي ( عند استيلائهم) وغلبتهم على الناس المخالفين لهم ( وطمسوا آثاره حتى انمحى بالكلية ) ومع قيام هذه الاحتمالات ) الثمانية ( لا يبقي لها أي للخارق الذي سمى معجزة ( دلالة على الصدق . الجواب الإجمالي ما قررناه غير مرة ) أي قررناه مراراً ومن جملتها جواب الطائفة الرابعة ( من أن التجويزات العقلية لا تنافي العلم العادي) كما في المحسوسات. (و) الجواب ( التفصيلي عن الأول أنا بينا أن لا مؤثرة في الوجود إلا الله فالمعجز لا يكون إلا فعلاً له لا للمدعي ) والسحر ونحوه إن لم يبلغ حد (الإعجاز الذي هو ( كفلق البحر وإحياء الموتى ) وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص ) كما هو مذهب جميع العقلاء فظاهر أنه لا يلتبس السحرة بالمعجزة فلا إشكال ( وإن بلغ ( السحر حد الإعجاز ( فإما ) أن يكون ( دون دعوى النبوة والتحدي فظاهر أيضاً أنه لا التباس (أو) يكون (معه) أي مع ادعاء النبوة والتحدي وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إما ) أن لا يخلقه الله على يده أو أن يقدر غيره على معارضته وإلا كان تصديقاً للكاذب وإنه محال ) على الله سبحانه لكونه كذباً . ( و ) الجواب ( عن الثاني أن لا خالق إلا الله فلا يكون المعجز مستنداً إلى غير ) وعن الثالث : إن ( لم يجوز الكرامة فلا إشكال عليه و ( من جوزها فقال بعضهم منهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق : لا تبلغ الكرامة الظاهرة على يد الأولياء (درجة المعجز، وقيل: لا تقع الكرامة ( على القصد والاختيار حتى إذا أراد الولي إيقاعها لم تقع بل وقوعها اتفاقي فقط ) وقال القاضي : تجوز الكرامة (إذ لم تقع على طريق التعظيم والجلال لأن ذلك ليس من شعار الصالحين ومع ذلك تمتاز ) الكرامة عن المعجز ( بأنها مع دعوى الولاية دون النبوة وعلى التقادير كلها ( فالفرق بينها وبين المعجزة ظاهر) فلا تشتبه إحداهما بالأخرى. وعن الرابع: إنا لا نقول بالغرض ) أي لأنا نقول بأن خلق المعجزة لغرض التصديق لأن أفعاله تعالى عندنا غير معللة بالأغراض ( بل نقول : ( إن خلقها على يد المدعي ( يدل على تصديق له قائم بذاته تعالى كما أن حمرة الخجل تفيد العلم الضروري بحصول الخجلة مع جواز حصولها بدونها أما على القول باستناد الحوادث إلى القادر المختار فظاهر وأما على القول بالموجب فلأنه يجوز أن يحدث شكل غريب سماوي يقتضي تلك الحمرة في ذلك الشخص من غير أن يحصل فيه الخجالة ( وعن الخامس : فقد مر في مسألة الكلام من موقف الإلهيات امتناع الكذب عليه سبحانه وتعالى . ( وعن السادس : إذا قوله : (وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إلخ ) يمكن أن يقال : لا حاجة إلى شيء منهما لجواز أن يخلق الله تعالى العلم الضروري بكذبه أو ينصب أمارات دالة على كذبه بحيث يعلم منها قطعاً .
قوله : (لا) تبلغ الكرامة درجة (المعجزة هذا مردود بأن من جملة المعجزات علم الغيب وإحياء الموتى، وقد روى مثل ذلك عن كثير من السلف. ولذا قيل إن الأمة مرآة نبيهم فما وقع معجزة للنبي عليه السلام صح مثله كرامة لأمته إذا كانت على طريقته .
The First Observatory - The Third Purpose: On the possibility of the mission. By that type of composition without other. (Second: Among those possibilities: its attribution, i.e., the attribution of the miracle to some angels, for they are capable of strange acts. Perhaps an angel manifested what humans are incapable of at the hand of the claimant to prophethood to mislead the people. As for the infallibility of angels, it is known only by scripture, so it cannot be relied upon here. Or to the devils, for they exist according to you, capable of extraordinary acts. Or its attribution to astrological conjunctions and their effects from the motions of the celestial spheres, and he (the claimant to prophethood) has encompassed the art of astrology beyond others, so he becomes aware of a rare conjunction that occurs only once in thousands of years and entails a strange event, and then he takes that which he knows will occur from among the strange events as a miracle for himself, so it is not then indicative of his truthfulness. (Third: Among them is that the apparent extraordinary act is a miracle of saints (karama) not a miracle (mu'jiza), so it has no indication of truthfulness. (Fourth: That the confirmation (tasdiq) is not accompanied by it, i.e., we grant that the miracle is from God, but it is not a confirmation from Him for the claimant, for there is no necessary purpose for the claimant, since there is no necessary purpose in His acts, and on the assumption of its necessity, the confirmation is not determined to be the purpose of that extraordinary act, for perhaps its purpose is other than confirmation, such as making it appear as confirmation so that one may be cautious of it through exertion and thus be rewarded, like the sending down of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat), for their apparent meanings suggest error, and the accountable person cannot avoid that error except by bearing the difficulty of precise reflection on them, thereby deserving reward. Or that extraordinary act is for confirming another prophet existing on another side, or it is a foretelling (irhas) for a prophet to come later, like the conditions appearing upon the prophet before his mission and the light that was on the foreheads of his ancestors. (Fifth: That the confirmation of God of him does not entail his truthfulness unless one knows that lying is impossible for God, and that is not known rationally (for according to you nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation due to circularity. (Sixth: Perhaps the challenge (tahaddi) issued by the claimant did not reach those capable of opposition among those in some regions, or perhaps the capable one abandoned it out of collusion with the claimant in promoting his word, so that his state would gain abundant fortune. (Seventh: Perhaps they underestimated him initially, thinking his call would not succeed and would not be paid attention to, so they did not occupy themselves with opposing him at the beginning of his affair, and they feared him later due to the severity of his power and the multitude of his followers, or they were occupied with what they needed for their livelihood away from him. (Eighth: Perhaps there were obstacles and the opponent did not appear due to a hindrance preventing him from showing his opposition, or he appeared and then his companions, i.e., the followers of the claimant, hid it when they prevailed and overcame the opposing people, and obliterated its traces until it was completely erased. And with the existence of these eight possibilities, there remains no indication of truthfulness for the extraordinary act called a miracle. The summary answer is what we have established more than once, i.e., we have established it repeatedly, including the answer of the fourth group: that rational possibilities do not contradict ordinary knowledge, as in sense-perceptibles. And the detailed answer to the first: we have shown that there is no effective agent in existence except God, so the miracle can only be an act of His, not of the claimant. And magic and the like, if they do not reach the level of inimitability (i'jaz) which is like splitting the sea and reviving the dead and healing the blind and leprous, as is the doctrine of all rational people, then it is apparent that magicians are not confused with miracle, so no problem. And if magic reaches the level of inimitability, then either it is without the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then it is also apparent that there is no confusion, or it is with it, i.e., with the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then one of two things is unavoidable: either God does not create it at his hand, or He empowers someone else to oppose it; otherwise, it would be confirmation of a liar, and that is impossible for God, being falsehood. And the answer to the second: there is no creator except God, so the miracle cannot be attributed to other than Him. And about the third: if one does not allow miracles of saints (karama), then no problem; and for those who allow it, some said, including al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq: the karama apparent at the hand of saints does not reach the degree of the miracle; and it was said: karama does not occur intentionally and voluntarily, such that if the saint wants to perform it, it does not happen, rather its occurrence is only accidental. And al-Qadi said: karama is allowed, since it does not occur in the way of glorification and majesty, because that is not the character of the righteous; nevertheless, the karama is distinguished from the mu'jiza by being with the claim of sainthood (wilaya) not prophethood. And according to all the positions, the difference between them and the miracle is apparent, so one is not confused with the other. And about the fourth: we do not say purpose, i.e., we do not say that the creation of the miracle is for the purpose of confirmation, because His acts are not caused by purposes according to us; rather we say: its creation at the hand of the claimant indicates a confirmation for him subsisting in God's essence, just as the redness of embarrassment yields necessary knowledge of the occurrence of embarrassment, even though it is possible for it to occur without it. This is clear on the doctrine of attributing events to the free chooser; as for the doctrine of necessitation (al-mujib), it is possible that a strange celestial figure occurs necessitating that redness in that person without the occurrence of embarrassment in him. And about the fifth: it has already passed in the issue of speech (kalam) from the stand of divinity the impossibility of lying upon Him, exalted and high. And about the sixth: then his saying: (Then one of two things is unavoidable, etc.) It can be said: there is no need for either of them, because it is possible that God creates necessary knowledge of his lying or sets up indicators indicating his lying such that one knows it definitively. His saying: (No) the karama reaches the degree of the miracle. This is refuted by the fact that among the miracles are knowledge of the unseen and reviving the dead, and that has been narrated from many of the predecessors. Hence it is said: the community is the mirror of their prophet, so whatever occurred as a miracle for the prophet, peace be upon him, its like is valid as a karama for his community if they are upon his path.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation of eight objections (shubuhāt) against the probative force of miracles (mu‘jizāt) in establishing the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood, followed by a general refutation and then detailed answers to each objection. The author first lists the objections sequentially:
1. (Second objection, since the first is on a previous page) The miracle might be attributable to angels or devils performing extraordinary acts, or to astrological knowledge enabling the claimant to predict a rare event.
2. The extraordinary act might be a saintly miracle (karāma) rather than a prophetic miracle.
3. The miracle does not necessarily carry God's confirmation (taṣdīq) because God has no necessary purpose; it could be meant to test people (like ambiguous verses) or to confirm another prophet or to be a foretelling.
4. God's confirmation does not entail the claimant's truthfulness unless we know that lying is impossible for God, which is not known rationally (since nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation (circular).
5. The challenge (taḥaddī) may not have reached capable opponents, or they colluded with the claimant.
6. People may have initially underestimated him and then feared his power, or were preoccupied.
7. Obstacles may have prevented opposition, or opponents' works were suppressed.
The objector concludes that with these possibilities, miracles lose their probative value.

The general answer (al-jawāb al-ijmālī) states that rational possibilities (tajwīzāt) do not negate ordinary certainty (al-‘ilm al-‘ādī), just as in the case of sense-perceptibles.

Then detailed answers follow:
- To the first: Only God is the true agent; magic, unless it reaches the level of inimitability and is claimed with challenge, does not confuse; if it does, God either prevents it or enables opposition, otherwise it would be confirming a liar, which is impossible.
- To the second: Only God creates; miracles cannot be from other than Him.
- To the third: If karāma is denied, no problem; if allowed, it is lesser or unintentional or not in a manner of glorification, and is distinct by being linked to sainthood not prophethood.
- To the fourth: Actions of God are not purpose-driven; the miracle indicates confirmation inherently, like blushing indicates embarrassment.
- To the fifth: The impossibility of lying about God has been established earlier.
- To the sixth: It is possible that God gives necessary knowledge of the claimant's falsity without needing opposition.
The passage ends with a marginal remark refuting the claim that karāma cannot reach the level of mu‘jiza, citing examples from the Salaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational possibilities completely destroy the certainty of miracles.
Correction: The general answer shows they only affect theoretical certainty, not the ordinary certainty we rely on.

Checkpoint
According to the general answer, rational possibilities do not negate ordinary knowledge because they are similar to which type of everyday certainty?
A) Mathematical truths
B) Sense-perceptibles
C) Historical reports
D) Logical necessities

Key Takeaway
The general answer establishes that rational possibilities do not undermine ordinary certainty, and the detailed refutations show the weaknesses of the first four objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear doubts about the miracles of the Prophet ﷺ — whether from external critics or internal whispers — do you treat those doubts as real threats to your faith, or do you trust the ordinary certainty that God has placed in your heart? What changes if you truly internalize that rational possibilities do not destroy that certainty?
?
The passage argues that a miracle is not for any purpose in God, but rather it inherently indicates confirmation, like a blush indicates embarrassment. Does your reliance on God's signs ever depend on you seeing a 'purpose' behind them? Would you still accept a miracle as a divine confirmation even if you could not explain why God did it?
?
Al-Qushji refutes the doubt that a miracle could be magic by saying that if magic reached the level of inimitability, God would either not create it or would send someone to oppose it. In your own life, when you see something that seems to challenge the truth of Islam, do you trust that God would not allow a definitive proof of falsehood to stand unchallenged? Or do you waver? What would it take for you to have that trust?

Detailed Refutations (Part 2) and Final Remark
Al-Qushji gives refutations of the last two doubts and adds a marginal comment on karama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutations of the fifth and sixth objections, and the marginal remark about the level of karama.

Core Idea
The refutations of the final objections rely on established doctrines and the possibility of direct divine knowledge.

Al-Qushji continues the detailed refutations, addressing the fifth and sixth objections. The fifth is already answered by the earlier discussion on God's inability to lie. The sixth is refuted by the possibility that God can create necessary knowledge of the claimant's falsity. Finally, a marginal remark defends the possibility of karama reaching the level of miracles, citing examples from the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of the fifth doubt
The answer refers to an earlier discussion on the impossibility of God lying. This shows the interconnectedness of kalam topics.
This is a cross-reference to the discussion on God's speech.
2
Read the refutation of the sixth doubt
The author argues that God can create immediate certain knowledge of the claimant's falsity, removing the need for opposition.
This refutes the objection that no one opposed the claimant.
3
Examine the final marginal remark on karama
This remark refutes the claim that karama cannot reach the level of mu'jiza, giving examples of similar acts by saints.
It also establishes the principle that the community is the mirror of the prophet.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة
بذلك النوع من التركيب دون غيره ( الثاني : ( من تلك الاحتمالات ( استناده) أي استناد المعجز ( إلى بعض الملائكة ) فإنها قادرة على أفعال غريبة فلعل ملكاً أظهر ما يعجز عنه البشر على يد المتنبي ليغوي الناس وأما عصمة الملائكة فإنما تعلم بقول فلا يمكن أن يتمسك بها هاهنا ) أو (الشياطين ) فإنها موجودة عندكم قادرة على أفعال خارقة ( أو ) استناده (إلى الاتصالات (الكوكبية ) وأنظارها الحادثة الحركات الفلكية (وهو) أي مدعي النبوة ( قد أحاط من صناعة النجامة بما لم يحط به غيره فاطلع على اتصال نادر لا يقع مثله إلا في ألوف من السنين ويستتبع أمراً غريباً ( فاتخذ ما علم وقوعه من الغرائب معجزاً لنفسه فلا يكون حينئذ دالاً على صدقه . ( الثالث : ( منها ( أن يكون ) الخارق الظاهر ) كرامة لا معجزة ) فلا يكون له دلالة على الصدق . ( الرابع : أن لا يصدق به التصديق ) أي سلمنا أن المعجز من تعالى لكنه ليس تصديقاً منه للمدعي ( إذ لا غرض واجباً ) للمدعي (إذ لا غرض واجباً) في أفعاله تعالى ( و) على تقدير وجوبه ( لا يتعين) التصديق له لكونه غرضاً من ذلك الخارق (إذ لعله ) أي الغرض منه ( غير التصديق ) له ( كإيهامه ) أي إيهام تصديقه ( ليحترز عنه بالاجتهاد فيثاب ) بذلك ) كإنزال المتشابهات ( فإنها بظواهرها توهم الخطأ ولا يمكن للمكلف الاحتراز عن ذلك الخطأ إلا بتحمل المشقة من التأمل الدقيق فيها فيستحق به الثواب ( أو ) يكون ذلك الخارق ( لتصديق نبي (آخر) موجود في جانب آخر أو يكون إرهاصاً لنبي سيأتي فيما بعد كالأحوال الظاهرة على النبي قبل مبعثه وكالنور الذي كان في جبين آبائه ( الخامس : أنه لا يلزم من تصديق الله ) إياه (صدقه إلا إذا علم استحالة الكذب على الله ولم يعلم ذلك عقلاً ( إذ لا يقبح عندكم منه شيء ) ولا سمعاً للزوم الدور السادس : لعل التحدي ) الصادر عن المدعي (لم يبلغ من هو قادر على المعارضة ) من الذين هم في بعض الأقطار، ( أو لعله ) أي القادر على المعارضة ( تركها مواضعة) مع المدعي ومواطأة معه ( في إعلاء كلمته لينال دولته حظاً) من وافراً . ( السابع : لعلهم استهانوا به (أولاً وظنوا أن دعوته مما لا يتم ولا يلتفت إليه فلم يشتغلوا بمعارضته في ابتداء أمره ) وخافوه آخر الشدة شوكته ) وكثرة أتباعه ( أو شغلهم ما يحتاجون إليه في تقويم معيشتهم عنه ) أي عن المدعي ومعارضته ( الثامن : لعله عوارض ولم يظهر لمانع منع المعارض عن إظهار ما عارض به ( أو ظهر ثم أخفاه أصحابه أي أتباع المدعي ( عند استيلائهم) وغلبتهم على الناس المخالفين لهم ( وطمسوا آثاره حتى انمحى بالكلية ) ومع قيام هذه الاحتمالات ) الثمانية ( لا يبقي لها أي للخارق الذي سمى معجزة ( دلالة على الصدق . الجواب الإجمالي ما قررناه غير مرة ) أي قررناه مراراً ومن جملتها جواب الطائفة الرابعة ( من أن التجويزات العقلية لا تنافي العلم العادي) كما في المحسوسات. (و) الجواب ( التفصيلي عن الأول أنا بينا أن لا مؤثرة في الوجود إلا الله فالمعجز لا يكون إلا فعلاً له لا للمدعي ) والسحر ونحوه إن لم يبلغ حد (الإعجاز الذي هو ( كفلق البحر وإحياء الموتى ) وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص ) كما هو مذهب جميع العقلاء فظاهر أنه لا يلتبس السحرة بالمعجزة فلا إشكال ( وإن بلغ ( السحر حد الإعجاز ( فإما ) أن يكون ( دون دعوى النبوة والتحدي فظاهر أيضاً أنه لا التباس (أو) يكون (معه) أي مع ادعاء النبوة والتحدي وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إما ) أن لا يخلقه الله على يده أو أن يقدر غيره على معارضته وإلا كان تصديقاً للكاذب وإنه محال ) على الله سبحانه لكونه كذباً . ( و ) الجواب ( عن الثاني أن لا خالق إلا الله فلا يكون المعجز مستنداً إلى غير ) وعن الثالث : إن ( لم يجوز الكرامة فلا إشكال عليه و ( من جوزها فقال بعضهم منهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق : لا تبلغ الكرامة الظاهرة على يد الأولياء (درجة المعجز، وقيل: لا تقع الكرامة ( على القصد والاختيار حتى إذا أراد الولي إيقاعها لم تقع بل وقوعها اتفاقي فقط ) وقال القاضي : تجوز الكرامة (إذ لم تقع على طريق التعظيم والجلال لأن ذلك ليس من شعار الصالحين ومع ذلك تمتاز ) الكرامة عن المعجز ( بأنها مع دعوى الولاية دون النبوة وعلى التقادير كلها ( فالفرق بينها وبين المعجزة ظاهر) فلا تشتبه إحداهما بالأخرى. وعن الرابع: إنا لا نقول بالغرض ) أي لأنا نقول بأن خلق المعجزة لغرض التصديق لأن أفعاله تعالى عندنا غير معللة بالأغراض ( بل نقول : ( إن خلقها على يد المدعي ( يدل على تصديق له قائم بذاته تعالى كما أن حمرة الخجل تفيد العلم الضروري بحصول الخجلة مع جواز حصولها بدونها أما على القول باستناد الحوادث إلى القادر المختار فظاهر وأما على القول بالموجب فلأنه يجوز أن يحدث شكل غريب سماوي يقتضي تلك الحمرة في ذلك الشخص من غير أن يحصل فيه الخجالة ( وعن الخامس : فقد مر في مسألة الكلام من موقف الإلهيات امتناع الكذب عليه سبحانه وتعالى . ( وعن السادس : إذا قوله : (وحينئذ فلا بد من أحد أمرين إلخ ) يمكن أن يقال : لا حاجة إلى شيء منهما لجواز أن يخلق الله تعالى العلم الضروري بكذبه أو ينصب أمارات دالة على كذبه بحيث يعلم منها قطعاً .
قوله : (لا) تبلغ الكرامة درجة (المعجزة هذا مردود بأن من جملة المعجزات علم الغيب وإحياء الموتى، وقد روى مثل ذلك عن كثير من السلف. ولذا قيل إن الأمة مرآة نبيهم فما وقع معجزة للنبي عليه السلام صح مثله كرامة لأمته إذا كانت على طريقته .
The First Observatory - The Third Purpose: On the possibility of the mission. By that type of composition without other. (Second: Among those possibilities: its attribution, i.e., the attribution of the miracle to some angels, for they are capable of strange acts. Perhaps an angel manifested what humans are incapable of at the hand of the claimant to prophethood to mislead the people. As for the infallibility of angels, it is known only by scripture, so it cannot be relied upon here. Or to the devils, for they exist according to you, capable of extraordinary acts. Or its attribution to astrological conjunctions and their effects from the motions of the celestial spheres, and he (the claimant to prophethood) has encompassed the art of astrology beyond others, so he becomes aware of a rare conjunction that occurs only once in thousands of years and entails a strange event, and then he takes that which he knows will occur from among the strange events as a miracle for himself, so it is not then indicative of his truthfulness. (Third: Among them is that the apparent extraordinary act is a miracle of saints (karama) not a miracle (mu'jiza), so it has no indication of truthfulness. (Fourth: That the confirmation (tasdiq) is not accompanied by it, i.e., we grant that the miracle is from God, but it is not a confirmation from Him for the claimant, for there is no necessary purpose for the claimant, since there is no necessary purpose in His acts, and on the assumption of its necessity, the confirmation is not determined to be the purpose of that extraordinary act, for perhaps its purpose is other than confirmation, such as making it appear as confirmation so that one may be cautious of it through exertion and thus be rewarded, like the sending down of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat), for their apparent meanings suggest error, and the accountable person cannot avoid that error except by bearing the difficulty of precise reflection on them, thereby deserving reward. Or that extraordinary act is for confirming another prophet existing on another side, or it is a foretelling (irhas) for a prophet to come later, like the conditions appearing upon the prophet before his mission and the light that was on the foreheads of his ancestors. (Fifth: That the confirmation of God of him does not entail his truthfulness unless one knows that lying is impossible for God, and that is not known rationally (for according to you nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation due to circularity. (Sixth: Perhaps the challenge (tahaddi) issued by the claimant did not reach those capable of opposition among those in some regions, or perhaps the capable one abandoned it out of collusion with the claimant in promoting his word, so that his state would gain abundant fortune. (Seventh: Perhaps they underestimated him initially, thinking his call would not succeed and would not be paid attention to, so they did not occupy themselves with opposing him at the beginning of his affair, and they feared him later due to the severity of his power and the multitude of his followers, or they were occupied with what they needed for their livelihood away from him. (Eighth: Perhaps there were obstacles and the opponent did not appear due to a hindrance preventing him from showing his opposition, or he appeared and then his companions, i.e., the followers of the claimant, hid it when they prevailed and overcame the opposing people, and obliterated its traces until it was completely erased. And with the existence of these eight possibilities, there remains no indication of truthfulness for the extraordinary act called a miracle. The summary answer is what we have established more than once, i.e., we have established it repeatedly, including the answer of the fourth group: that rational possibilities do not contradict ordinary knowledge, as in sense-perceptibles. And the detailed answer to the first: we have shown that there is no effective agent in existence except God, so the miracle can only be an act of His, not of the claimant. And magic and the like, if they do not reach the level of inimitability (i'jaz) which is like splitting the sea and reviving the dead and healing the blind and leprous, as is the doctrine of all rational people, then it is apparent that magicians are not confused with miracle, so no problem. And if magic reaches the level of inimitability, then either it is without the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then it is also apparent that there is no confusion, or it is with it, i.e., with the claim of prophethood and challenge, and then one of two things is unavoidable: either God does not create it at his hand, or He empowers someone else to oppose it; otherwise, it would be confirmation of a liar, and that is impossible for God, being falsehood. And the answer to the second: there is no creator except God, so the miracle cannot be attributed to other than Him. And about the third: if one does not allow miracles of saints (karama), then no problem; and for those who allow it, some said, including al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq: the karama apparent at the hand of saints does not reach the degree of the miracle; and it was said: karama does not occur intentionally and voluntarily, such that if the saint wants to perform it, it does not happen, rather its occurrence is only accidental. And al-Qadi said: karama is allowed, since it does not occur in the way of glorification and majesty, because that is not the character of the righteous; nevertheless, the karama is distinguished from the mu'jiza by being with the claim of sainthood (wilaya) not prophethood. And according to all the positions, the difference between them and the miracle is apparent, so one is not confused with the other. And about the fourth: we do not say purpose, i.e., we do not say that the creation of the miracle is for the purpose of confirmation, because His acts are not caused by purposes according to us; rather we say: its creation at the hand of the claimant indicates a confirmation for him subsisting in God's essence, just as the redness of embarrassment yields necessary knowledge of the occurrence of embarrassment, even though it is possible for it to occur without it. This is clear on the doctrine of attributing events to the free chooser; as for the doctrine of necessitation (al-mujib), it is possible that a strange celestial figure occurs necessitating that redness in that person without the occurrence of embarrassment in him. And about the fifth: it has already passed in the issue of speech (kalam) from the stand of divinity the impossibility of lying upon Him, exalted and high. And about the sixth: then his saying: (Then one of two things is unavoidable, etc.) It can be said: there is no need for either of them, because it is possible that God creates necessary knowledge of his lying or sets up indicators indicating his lying such that one knows it definitively. His saying: (No) the karama reaches the degree of the miracle. This is refuted by the fact that among the miracles are knowledge of the unseen and reviving the dead, and that has been narrated from many of the predecessors. Hence it is said: the community is the mirror of their prophet, so whatever occurred as a miracle for the prophet, peace be upon him, its like is valid as a karama for his community if they are upon his path.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation of eight objections (shubuhāt) against the probative force of miracles (mu‘jizāt) in establishing the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood, followed by a general refutation and then detailed answers to each objection. The author first lists the objections sequentially:
1. (Second objection, since the first is on a previous page) The miracle might be attributable to angels or devils performing extraordinary acts, or to astrological knowledge enabling the claimant to predict a rare event.
2. The extraordinary act might be a saintly miracle (karāma) rather than a prophetic miracle.
3. The miracle does not necessarily carry God's confirmation (taṣdīq) because God has no necessary purpose; it could be meant to test people (like ambiguous verses) or to confirm another prophet or to be a foretelling.
4. God's confirmation does not entail the claimant's truthfulness unless we know that lying is impossible for God, which is not known rationally (since nothing is evil from Him) nor by revelation (circular).
5. The challenge (taḥaddī) may not have reached capable opponents, or they colluded with the claimant.
6. People may have initially underestimated him and then feared his power, or were preoccupied.
7. Obstacles may have prevented opposition, or opponents' works were suppressed.
The objector concludes that with these possibilities, miracles lose their probative value.

The general answer (al-jawāb al-ijmālī) states that rational possibilities (tajwīzāt) do not negate ordinary certainty (al-‘ilm al-‘ādī), just as in the case of sense-perceptibles.

Then detailed answers follow:
- To the first: Only God is the true agent; magic, unless it reaches the level of inimitability and is claimed with challenge, does not confuse; if it does, God either prevents it or enables opposition, otherwise it would be confirming a liar, which is impossible.
- To the second: Only God creates; miracles cannot be from other than Him.
- To the third: If karāma is denied, no problem; if allowed, it is lesser or unintentional or not in a manner of glorification, and is distinct by being linked to sainthood not prophethood.
- To the fourth: Actions of God are not purpose-driven; the miracle indicates confirmation inherently, like blushing indicates embarrassment.
- To the fifth: The impossibility of lying about God has been established earlier.
- To the sixth: It is possible that God gives necessary knowledge of the claimant's falsity without needing opposition.
The passage ends with a marginal remark refuting the claim that karāma cannot reach the level of mu‘jiza, citing examples from the Salaf.

Key Terms
كذب
علم ضروري
إرهاص
أمة مرآة نبيها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Karama cannot be as great as a prophetic miracle.
Correction: The marginal remark shows that similar acts have been reported from saints, so karama can reach that level.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation of the sixth doubt, what alternative does God have to ensure the claimant's falsity is known?
A) He sends another prophet
B) He creates necessary knowledge or sets up clear indicators
C) He allows the opponents to triumph
D) He reveals a book

Key Takeaway
The final refutations rely on earlier theological proofs and the possibility of direct divine intervention to expose false claimants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says the community is the mirror of the prophet. Look at your own life: what does your mirror reflect? If others saw only your actions, would they see the Prophet's path? What one habit do you need to change today to better mirror him?
?
If God can directly expose false claimants, why do you still hesitate to fully trust the truthful claims of Islam? What is holding you back from submitting completely to the One who cannot lie?
?
The early saints performed miracles like reviving the dead through their closeness to Allah. Do you truly believe that such possibility exists for you if you follow the Prophet's path? What would change in your worship if you lived with that conviction?

The First Argument: The Possibility of Lying in the Whole
First argument: individual possibility implies collective possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument against tawatur yielding certainty: that since each individual may lie, the whole group may also lie.

Core Idea
The whole is composed of individuals; if each can lie, so can the whole.

The deniers of prophethood argue that tawatur cannot produce certain knowledge of miracles. Their first argument is straightforward: if it is possible for each individual transmitter to lie, then it is possible for the entire group to lie, since the group is nothing but the sum of its individuals. This passage presents that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the argument's rhythm come through.
The argument is very concise; note the phrase 'ليس كذب الكل إلا كذب كل واحد'.
2
Identify the logical structure
The passage moves from a premise (each individual can lie) to a conclusion (the whole can lie). Identify these two parts.
The conclusion is presented as a direct consequence: 'فكذا الكل يجوز عليه الكذب'.
3
Reflect on the implication for tawatur
If the whole can lie, then tawatur does not guarantee truth. Consider why this argument alone might be insufficient – the commentary will help.
Think about how one might object: does the possibility of lying in each individual necessarily transfer to the collective?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة (السادسة : ) من منكري البعثة ( من قال : العلم بحصول المعجز لا يمكن لمن لم يشاهده إلا بالتواتر ولكنه لا يفيد العلم ) فلا يحصل العلم بنبوة أحد لمن لم يشاهد ،معجزة، وإنما قلنا : إن التواتر لا يفيد العلم ( لوجوه : الأول : أهل التواتر يجوز الكذب على كل واحد منهم فكذا الكل يجوز عليه الكذب ( إذ ليس كذب الكل إلا كذب كل واحد. الثاني : إن حكم كل (طبقة ) من طبقات أعداد الرواة ( حكم ما قبلها بواحد فإن من جوز إفادة المائة للعلم جوز إفادة التسعة والتسعين له قطعاً، ولم يحصره ) أي العلم ( في عدد معين (و) أيضاً ( ادعاء الفرق ) بين العددين المذكورين في إفادة العلم ( تحكم) محض ، وإذا كان كذلك ( فلنفرض طبقة لا تفيده ) أي لا تفيد العلم قطعاً كاثنين مثلاً ( ثم نزيد عليه واحداً واحداً فلا يفيده) شيء من هذه المراتب (بالغاً ما بلغ المساواة كل منها لما قيل في عدم الإفادة. ( الثالث : لو أوجب التواتر العلم لأوجبه خبر الواحد واللازم منتف) اتفاقا ( بيان الملازمة أن التواتر لا يشترط فيه قوله : (بيان الملازمة أن التواتر (إلخ يمكن بيان الملازمة بمثل ما سبق من أن حكم كل طبيعة حكم ما قبلها فإذا أفاد المئة أفاد التسعة والتسعون، وإذا أفاد هذا أفاد الثمانية والتسعون إلى أن يبلغ الواحد .
The sixth group of deniers of prophethood (who said: Knowledge of the occurrence of a miracle is not possible for one who did not witness it except through tawatur, but it does not yield knowledge, so knowledge of the prophethood of anyone is not obtained for one who did not witness a miracle. And we said: Tawatur does not yield knowledge due to several reasons: First: It is possible for each one of the people of tawatur to lie, so similarly it is possible for the whole group to lie, because the lie of the whole is nothing but the lie of each individual. Second: The ruling of each (level) of the levels of the number of narrators is the ruling of what is one less than it. For if one permits that a hundred yields knowledge, one permits that ninety-nine yields it definitely, and it is not restricted to a specific number. And also claiming a difference between the two mentioned numbers in yielding knowledge is pure arbitrariness. And if this is so, then let us suppose a level that does not yield it, definitely cut off, like two, then we add one by one, and none of these levels yields it, no matter how far it goes, because each is equal to what was said about non-yielding. Third: If tawatur necessitated knowledge, then a single report would necessitate it, and the consequent is false by consensus. The explanation of the implication is that tawatur does not require... (marginal note: (The explanation of the implication that tawatur) can be made by the same reasoning as before that the ruling of each nature is the ruling of what is before it. So if a hundred yields, then ninety-nine yields, and if this yields, then eighty-eight yields, until reaching one.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage presents the arguments of the sixth group who deny that tawatur (mass transmission) yields knowledge of a miracle one did not witness. They give three arguments: (1) Since each individual can lie, the whole group can lie, as the whole is composed of individuals. (2) If tawatur yields knowledge only from a certain number, it is arbitrary; if from any number, then adding individuals gradually would never reach certainty. (3) If tawatur yielded knowledge, then a single report would also, which is false. The marginal note shows how to establish the implication: by the same logic used earlier, that if a larger number yields, then each smaller number yields by parity, eventually reaching one.

Key Terms
تواتر
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If many people transmit a report, it must be true because they cannot all be liars.
Correction: The deniers argue that if each individual can lie, then the whole group can lie, so numbers alone do not eliminate the possibility of falsehood.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, why does tawatur not yield knowledge?
A) Because the chain may be broken
B) Because each member can lie, so the whole can lie
C) Because numbers are arbitrary
D) Because miracles are not verifiable

Key Takeaway
The first argument asserts that the possibility of lying in each individual implies the possibility of lying in the whole group, thus tawatur does not yield certainty.

The Second Argument: The Arbitrariness of the Required Number
Second argument: the ruling of each level is the same, making any specific number arbitrary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument: that tawatur's requirement of a minimum number is arbitrary and cannot be justified.

Core Idea
If one number yields certainty, then any number greater or lesser should also yield it, leading to contradiction.

The second argument targets the idea that tawatur yields knowledge only when a certain number of transmitters is reached. The deniers argue that if a certain number (like 100) yields knowledge, then 99 should also yield it, and so on, making the requirement arbitrary. This passage explains that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the key claim: 'حكم كل طبقة حكم ما قبلها'.
The logic relies on the equality of rulings across levels.
2
Follow the reductio
Start with a number that is thought to yield knowledge (e.g., 100). According to the principle, 99 should also yield. Extend this downward until you reach a number that clearly does not yield (e.g., 2). Contradiction.
The deniers conclude that no definite number yields knowledge.
3
Consider the idea of arbitrariness
The deniers claim that any specific number is arbitrary; there is no principled way to pick one number over another.
This challenges the common view that tawatur requires a minimum threshold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How do you personally determine that the transmission is reliable? What would it do to your certainty if you learned that the number of transmitters was arbitrary?
?
Have you ever dismissed a testimony because there weren't enough witnesses? On what basis did you set that number? The deniers argue that any number is arbitrary—does that resonate with your experience, or do you think there is a non-arbitrary threshold?
?
If human reasoning alone cannot settle the number required for certain knowledge, how does that highlight your need for divine guidance to establish truth? Could your reliance on 'enough evidence' be a form of hidden assumption that needs re-examination?
